**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Task: Kubelet Container Manager Architecture Guide

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0 (mirror of kubernetes/kubernetes) (stripped snapshot)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Objective

Produce a subsystem architecture guide for kubelet container manager, including resource manager interactions and platform variance.

## Scope

Focus on the kubelet container manager subsystem.
Your document must explain component responsibilities, end-to-end flow, and extension or operational tradeoffs.

## Content Expectations

Address all of the following in your own structure:
- subsystem purpose, boundaries, and upstream/downstream dependencies
- key components and how responsibilities are split
- end-to-end control/request flow with concrete repository evidence
- failure modes, limits, and design tradeoffs
- extension points, customization hooks, and associated risks
- a concise map of the most important files/directories used in your analysis

## Quality Bar

- Cite concrete file paths from the repository.
- Explain behavior and interactions, not just API signatures.
- Include at least one section on operational implications (performance, reliability, or maintainability).
- Do not fabricate classes, functions, or files.

## Anti-Requirements

- Do not output `doc.go`.
- Do not provide shallow bullet dumps without system flow explanation.
- Do not rely on external docs not present in the workspace.

262026-03-11T17:51:50.131071agentmessage-
I am thinking...: I now have enough information to write a comprehensive architecture guide. Let me organize what I've learned:

1. **ContainerManager interface** (`pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go`): The central interface. It manages:
   - Cgroup hierarchy setup and enforcement
   - Resource allocation (devices, CPUs, memory, DRA)
   - Node Allocatable computation and enforcement
   - QoS container hierarchy management
   - Plugin registration (Device Plugin, DRA)
   - PodResources API backend

2. **Platform implementations**:
   - Linux: `container_manager_linux.go` - full implementation with cgroups, cpumanager, memorymanager, topologymanager, devicemanager, DRA manager
   - Windows: `container_manager_windows.go` - similar but no cgroup hierarchy; CPU/memory affinity behind `WindowsCPUAndMemoryAffinity` feature gate; uses fake managers by default
   - Unsupported: `container_manager_unsupported.go` - returns error on Start()
   - Stub: `container_manager_stub.go` - no-op implementation for testing

3. **cgroup hierarchy** (Linux only):
   - `cgroup_manager_linux.go`: CgroupManager interface with Create/Destroy/Update/Validate/Exists
   - `cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go` and `cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go`: v1/v2 implementations
   - cgroup v1 is deprecated (CgroupV1DeprecatedWarning in container_manager.go line 52)
   - Node hierarchy: `/kubepods` (root) → `/kubepods/burstable`, `/kubepods/besteffort` → `pod<uid>` → individual containers
   - `node_container_manager_linux.go`: Creates and enforces the `/kubepods` node allocatable cgroup
   - `qos_container_manager_linux.go`: Creates and maintains QoS tier cgroups (burstable, besteffort), runs periodic updates every 1 minute
   - `pod_container_manager_linux.go`: Creates per-pod cgroup under QoS tier; on destruction, kil
... (truncated)

---

## What the document covers

**Section 1 — Purpose, boundaries, and dependencies**  
Maps the container manager's upstream inputs (cadvisor, CRI runtime, API server, plugin manager) and downstream consumers (kuberuntime, eviction, PodResources API, node status), grounded in the `Kubelet` struct fields in `pkg/kubelet/kubelet.go` and the `ContainerManager` interface imports.

**Section 2 — Key components and responsibilities**  
Covers all nine sub-components with their interface definitions and concrete implementations:
- `CgroupManager` (v1/v2 split, systemd/cgroupfs name translation)
- `QOSContainerManager` (1-minute periodic CPU-share and memory-limit reconciliation)
- `PodContainerManager` (per-pod cgroup CRUD, 5-retry process killing)
- CPU Manager (none/static policies, state persistence, reconcile loop)
- Memory Manager (NUMA-aware, mirrors CPU manager structure)
- Topology Manager (HintProvider aggregation, 8-NUMA-node hard limit, admission gating)
- Device Manager and DRA Manager

**Section 3 — End-to-end control flow**  
Traces initialization order in `Start()` (all 11 steps with line references to `container_manager_linux.go`), then admission → container creation → container start → teardown, showing exactly which interface methods are called and in what order.

**Section 4 — Failure modes, limits, and tradeoffs**  
Documents hard startup failures (missing cgroups, swap, >8 NUMA nodes), soft admission failures (`TopologyAffinityError`, `SMTAlignmentError`), runtime degradation paths (retry goroutines, reconcile drift), and the key design tradeoffs (noop fallback silences misconfigurations, 1-minute QoS staleness

}\\\\n836: \\\\n837: // getContainer returns the cgroup associated with the specified pid.\\\\n838: // It enforces a unified hierarchy for memory and cpu cgroups.\\\\n839: // On systemd environments, Let me organize what I've learned:\n\n1. **ContainerManager interface** (`pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go`): The central interface. It manages:\n   - Cgroup hierarchy setup and enforcement\n   - Resource allocation (devices, CPUs, memory, DRA)\n   - Node Allocatable computation and enforcement\n   - QoS container hierarchy management\n   - Plugin registration (Device Plugin, DRA)\n   - PodResources API backend\n\n2. **Platform implementations**:\n   - Linux: `container_manager_linux.go` - full implementation with cgroups, cpumanager, memorymanager, topologymanager, devicemanager, DRA manager\n   - Windows: `container_manager_windows.go` - similar but no cgroup hierarchy; CPU/memory affinity behind `WindowsCPUAndMemoryAffinity` feature gate; uses fake managers by default\n   - Unsupported: `container_manager_unsupported.go` - returns error on Start()\n   - Stub: `container_manager_stub.go` - no-op implementation for testing\n\n3. **cgroup hierarchy** (Linux only):\n   - `cgroup_manager_linux.go`: CgroupManager interface with Create/Destroy/Update/Validate/Exists\n   - `cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go` and `cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go`: v1/v2 implementations\n   - cgroup v1 is deprecated (CgroupV1DeprecatedWarning in container_manager.go line 52)\n   - Node hierarchy: `/kubepods` (root) \u2192 `/kubepods/burstable`, `/kubepods/besteffort` \u2192 `pod<uid>` \u2192 individual containers\n   - `node_container_manager_linux.go`: Creates and enforces the `/kubepods` node allocatable cgroup\n   - `qos_container_manager_linux.go`: Creates and maintains QoS tier cgroups (burstable, besteffort), runs periodic updates every 1 minute\n   - `pod_container_manager_linux.go`: Creates per-pod cgroup under QoS tier; on destruction, kills all processes with up to 5 retries\n\n4. **Resource managers**:\n   - **CPU Manager** (`cm/cpumanager/cpu_manager.go`): \n     - Interface: Allocate, AddContainer, RemoveContainer, Start\n     - Policies: `none` (shared pool only), `static` (exclusive integer CPUs for Guaranteed pods)\n     - State persisted to `cpu_manager_state` file\n     - Reconcile loop runs periodically\n   - **Memory Manager** (`cm/memorymanager/memory_manager.go`):\n     - Similar structure to CPU manager\n     - NUMA-aware memory allocation for Guaranteed pods\n   - **Topology Manager** (`cm/topologymanager/topology_manager.go`):\n     - Coordinates resource alignment via HintProvider interface\n     - DeviceManager, CPUManager, MemoryManager all register as HintProviders\n     - Policies: none, best-effort, restricted, single-numa-node\n     - Scopes: container, pod\n     - Hard limit: 8 NUMA nodes maximum\n     - Acts as PodAdmitHandler (via lifecycle.PodAdmitHandler)\n   - **Device Manager** (`cm/devicemanager/`): Manages device plugin resources\n   - **DRA Manager** (`cm/dra/`): Dynamic Resource Allocation (feature-gated)\n\n5. **InternalContainerLifecycle** (`internal_container_lifecycle.go`):\n   - Called at container lifecycle hooks: PreCreateContainer, PreStartContainer, PostStopContainer\n   - PreCreateContainer (Linux): sets CpusetCpus from CPUManager, CpusetMems from MemoryManager\n   - PreStartContainer: calls cpuManager.AddContainer, memoryManager.AddContainer, topologyManager.AddContainer\n   - PostStopContainer: calls topologyManager.RemoveContainer\n\n6. **Start() sequence** (Linux):\n   - Build container map from runtime\n   - Start DRA manager (if feature enabled)\n   - Start CPU manager\n   - Start memory manager\n   - Cache node info + ephemeral storage capacity\n   - Validate node allocatable\n   - setupNode(): validate system requirements, kernel tunables, create node allocatable cgroups, start QOS containers, enforce Node Allocatable, set up system containers (system cgroup, kubelet cgroup)\n   - Run housekeeping goroutines for system containers (every 1 minute) and periodic tasks (every 5 minutes)\n   - Start device manager\n\n7. **NodeConfig** (`container_manager.go`): Configuration struct including:\n   - CgroupsPerQOS, CgroupRoot, CgroupDriver (systemd or cgroupfs)\n   - CPUManagerPolicy, MemoryManagerPolicy, TopologyManagerPolicy/Scope\n   - NodeAllocatableConfig (KubeReserved, SystemReserved, EnforceNodeAllocatable, HardEvictionThresholds)\n   - EnforceCPULimits, CPUCFSQuotaPeriod\n\n8. **Resource accounting helpers** (`helpers_linux.go`):\n   - MinShares=2, MaxShares=262144, SharesPerCPU=1024\n   - MilliCPUToQuota: converts milliCPU to CFS quota (100ms period default)\n   - MilliCPUToShares: converts milliCPU to CPU shares\n\n9. **QoS manager** (`qos_container_manager_linux.go`):\n   - UpdateCgroups: runs every 1 minute, updates CPU shares and memory limits for QoS tiers\n   - setCPUCgroupConfig: sums CPU requests of Burstable pods to set shares\n   - setMemoryReserve: calculates memory limits based on --qos-reserved percentage\n   - retrySetMemoryReserve: if current usage > attempted limit, sets limit to current usage\n\n10. **Key failure modes**:\n    - Missing cgroup subsystems (cpu, cpuacct, cpuset, memory required on v1) \u2192 startup failure\n    - swap enabled with failSwapOn=true \u2192 startup failure\n    - >8 NUMA nodes \u2192 topology manager initialization fails\n    - cpumanager static policy, non-integer CPU request \u2192 SMTAlignmentError at admission\n    - TopologyAffinityError \u2192 pod admission rejected\n\n11. **Windows platform**:\n    - No cgroup hierarchy (no QOS/pod container managers)\n    - {
  "command": "create",
  "file_text": "# Kubelet Container Manager: Subsystem Architecture Guide\n\n## 1. Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\nThe **container manager** (`pkg/kubelet/cm`) is the kubelet subsystem responsible for translating Kubernetes resource semantics\u2014CPU, memory, devices, NUMA topology\u2014into kernel-level enforcement. It sits between the kubelet's pod lifecycle machinery and the Linux cgroup/CRI layer, answering three questions on every pod:\n\n1. **What may this pod consume?** (resource accounting, admission)\n2. **Where must it run?** (NUMA/topology placement, CPU pinning)\n3. **What extended hardware does it need?** (device plugins, DRA)\n\n### Upstream dependencies (inputs)\n\n| Source | What it provides |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/kubelet/kubelet.go` | Wires `cm.ContainerManager` into `Kubelet.containerManager`; calls `Start()` once and then calls lifecycle methods per pod/container |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cadvisor` | Machine topology (`MachineInfo()`), root filesystem info |\n| `k8s.io/cri-api/pkg/apis` (`RuntimeService`) | Live container map at start; `UpdateContainerResources()` for CPU reconciliation |\n| API Server / `clientset` | Used by DRA manager to watch `ResourceSlice` and `ResourceClaim` objects |\n| `pkg/kubelet/pluginmanager` | Delivers device-plugin socket registrations via `PluginHandler` |\n| `pkg/kubelet/lifecycle` | `PodAdmitHandler` interface; the topology manager implements this to gate pod admission |\n\n### Downstream outputs\n\n| Consumer | What it receives |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime` | `RunContainerOptions` (device mounts/envs/CDI devices) via `GetResources()`; CPU/memory affinity written into `ContainerConfig` via `InternalContainerLifecycle` |\n| `pkg/kubelet/eviction` | Node allocatable values used for eviction thresholds |\n| `pkg/kubelet/server` (PodResources API) | CPU, device, memory, DRA data via `CPUsProvider`, `DevicesProvider`, `MemoryProvider`, `DynamicResourcesProvider` interfaces |\n| `pkg/kubelet/nodestatus` | `GetCapacity()`, `GetDevicePluginResourceCapacity()`, `GetNodeAllocatableReservation()` |\n| Linux kernel cgroup filesystem | Cgroup directories, quota files, CPU shares, memory limits |\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\nThe subsystem is a single Go package (`pkg/kubelet/cm`) that composes six major sub-managers. Each has a narrow Go interface and the `ContainerManager` orchestrates them.\n\n### 2.1 `ContainerManager` (the orchestrator)\n\n**Interface**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go`, type `ContainerManager`\n\n`containerManagerImpl` (Linux) holds references to all sub-managers and is the only type exposed to the rest of the kubelet:\n\n```go\n// pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go:100-140\ntype containerManagerImpl struct {\n    sync.RWMutex\n    cadvisorInterface cadvisor.Interface\n    cgroupManager     CgroupManager\n    qosContainerManager QOSContainerManager\n    deviceManager     devicemanager.Manager\n    cpuManager        cpumanager.Manager\n    memoryManager     memorymanager.Manager\n    topologyManager   topologymanager.Manager\n    draManager        *dra.Manager\n    // ...\n}\n```\n\nIts responsibilities include:\n- Construction and sequential initialization of all sub-managers\n- Kernel tunable validation (`setupKernelTunables`, `ProtectKernelDefaults`)\n- Cgroup root setup and Node Allocatable enforcement\n- Fanning-in resource-update channels from device manager and DRA manager\n- Exposing the PodResources API data plane\n\n### 2.2 `CgroupManager`\n\n**Interface**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go`, type `CgroupManager`  \n**Implementations**: `cgroup_manager_linux.go` (shared), `cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go`, `cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go`\n\nPerforms the raw cgroup operations: `Create`, `Destroy`, `Update`, `Validate`, `Exists`, `MemoryUsage`, `Pids`, and `ReduceCPULimits`. Its `Name()` method translates the internal `CgroupName` (a `[]string` slice like `[\"kubepods\",\"burstable\",\"pod<uid>\"]`) into the driver-specific filesystem path. For the systemd driver it uses `cgroupsystemd.ExpandSlice()` to produce `/kubepods.slice/kubepods-burstable.slice/kubepods-burstable-pod<uid>.slice`; for the cgroupfs driver it joins with `/`.\n\nThe `NewCgroupManager` factory selects `cgroupV1impl` or `cgroupV2impl` based on `cgroups.IsCgroup2UnifiedMode()`. Cgroup v1 is actively deprecated\u2014a warning is emitted at startup:\n\n```go\n// pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go:52\nCgroupV1DeprecatedWarning = \"cgroup v1 detected. cgroup v1 support is deprecated...\"\n```\n\n### 2.3 `QOSContainerManager`\n\n**Interface**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/qos_container_manager_linux.go`, type `QOSContainerManager`  \n**Implementation**: `qosContainerManagerImpl`\n\nCreates and maintains the three top-level QoS tier cgroups under the cgroup root. The Guaranteed tier lives *at* the cgroup root itself; Burstable and BestEffort each get a child:\n\n```\n/kubepods            \u2190 Guaranteed (= cgroupRoot)\n/kubepods/burstable\n/kubepods/besteffort\n```\n\nOn startup it creates any missing QoS cgroups and then launches a goroutine that calls `UpdateCgroups` every `1 minute` (`periodicQOSCgroupUpdateInterval`). Each update recomputes:\n\n- **CPU shares** for Burstable: sums all Burstable pod CPU requests; `MilliCPUToShares()` converts them (`SharesPerCPU = 1024` per CPU, `MinShares = 2`).\n- **Memory limits** (when `QOSReserved` feature is enabled): calculates tier memory limits as `allocatable \u2212 (guaranteed_requests \u00d7 percentReserve / 100)` with a retry mechanism that raises the limit to current usage if the cgroup is already over the desired limit.\n- **MemoryQoS** (`memory.min`, cgroup v2 only, `MemoryQoS` feature): sets `memory.min` to prevent the OS from reclaiming memory below the sum of all pod requests in the tier.\n\n### 2.4 `PodContainerManager`\n\n**Interface**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go`, type `PodContainerManager`  \n**Linux implementation**: `pod_container_manager_linux.go`, type `podContainerManagerImpl`  \n**Fallback**: `podContainerManagerNoop` (when `CgroupsPerQOS=false`)\n\nThe pod workers call `EnsureExists()` before starting containers and `Destroy()` when a pod terminates. `EnsureExists` computes the pod cgroup name as `<QOS-parent>/pod<uid>`, derives a `ResourceConfig` from the pod spec via `ResourceConfigForPod()` (CPU shares, quota, memory limits, PID limits), and calls `cgroupManager.Create()`. Destruction first kills all processes attached to the cgroup with up to five retry rounds, then removes the cgroup.\n\nA key feature interaction: if `DisableCPUQuotaWithExclusiveCPUs` is enabled and the pod has pinned CPUs (checked via `ContainerManager.PodHasExclusiveCPUs()`), `EnsureExists` disables CFS quota for that pod cgroup, preventing quota interference with pinned workloads.\n\n### 2.5 CPU Manager\n\n**Interface**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/cpu_manager.go`, type `Manager`  \n**Implementation**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/cpu_manager.go`, type `manager`\n\nManages CPU affinity for containers through a pluggable policy:\n\n- **`none` policy** (`policy_none.go`): All containers use the shared CPU pool. All topology hints report no preference.\n- **`static` policy** (`policy_static.go`): Guaranteed pods requesting an integer number of CPUs receive exclusively dedicated logical CPUs. Containers from all other classes share the remaining pool. The static policy also supports SMT-alignment: it can require requests to be multiples of threads-per-core (`full-pcpus-only` option).\n\nState (the `podUID \u2192 containerName \u2192 CPUSet` mapping) is persisted to `cpu_manager_state` in `KubeletRootDir` so that CPU allocations survive kubelet restarts. A periodic reconcile loop calls `UpdateContainerResources()` on the CRI to push the current CPUSet into every container's cgroup, healing any drift.\n\nThe CPU manager implements `topologymanager.HintProvider`; when the topology manager calls `GetTopologyHints()`, the CPU manager returns possible NUMA-local CPU sets as bitmasks.\n\n### 2.6 Memory Manager\n\n**Interface**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/`, type `Manager`  \n**Implementation**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/memory_manager.go`\n\nMirrors the CPU manager's structure for NUMA-aware memory allocation. For Guaranteed pods it pins memory to specific NUMA nodes by writing `cpuset.mems` into the container's cgroup. State is also persisted to disk. It implements `HintProvider` and cooperates with the topology manager on placement decisions.\n\n### 2.7 Topology Manager\n\n**Interface**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/topology_manager.go`, type `Manager`  \n**Implementation**: `topology_manager.go` + `scope.go` + policy files\n\nThe topology manager acts as an **admission controller** for NUMA alignment. It implements `lifecycle.PodAdmitHandler`, meaning it is called during pod admission (`GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()` returns it).\n\nAt admission time it:\n1. Calls `GetTopologyHints(pod, container)` on every registered `HintProvider` (device manager, CPU manager, memory manager).\n2. Intersects the returned bitmask sets using the configured policy.\n3. Calls `Allocate(pod, container)` on each provider to commit resources matching the agreed hint.\n\nPolicies:\n- `none`: alignment is not enforced; hints are ignored.\n- `best-effort`: prefers aligned placement; admits the pod even if alignment is impossible.\n- `restricted`: only admits pods that can be placed with NUMA affinity.\n- `single-numa-node`: only admits pods whose resources all fit on a single NUMA node.\n\nScopes (`container` / `pod`) control whether alignment is computed per container or across the whole pod. The `noneScope` is used when the policy is `none`.\n\n**Hard limit**: The topology manager refuses to initialize on machines with more than 8 NUMA nodes because the hint enumeration would produce a state explosion (`defaultMaxAllowableNUMANodes = 8`).\n\n### 2.8 Device Manager\n\n**Directory**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/`\n\nManages device plugin registrations, allocations, and health monitoring. Exposes `GetWatcherHandler()` (registered with the plugin manager) and `GetCapacity()` (feeds node status). Device allocations are bundled into `RunContainerOptions` by `GetResources()`.\n\n### 2.9 DRA Manager\n\n**Directory**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/dra/`  \n**Feature gate**: `DynamicResourceAllocation`\n\nImplements the newer structured resource allocation model. Communicates with DRA drivers via gRPC and stores claim state in checkpoints. Exposes a `GetWatcherHandler()` similar to the device manager.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control Flow\n\n### 3.1 Initialization (`Start()`)\n\n`containerManagerImpl.Start()` is called once from `Kubelet.Run()` after the node is registered. The Linux sequence (`pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go:615`):\n\n```\n1. buildContainerMapAndRunningSetFromRuntime()      // enumerate live containers via CRI\n2. draManager.Start()                               // if DynamicResourceAllocation enabled\n3. cpuManager.Start()                               // loads persisted state, starts reconcile loop\n4. memoryManager.Start()                            // loads persisted state, starts reconcile loop\n5. cm.nodeInfo = node                               // cache node object\n6. cadvisor.RootFsInfo() \u2192 cm.capacity              // populate ephemeral-storage capacity\n7. validateNodeAllocatable()                         // sanity-check kube/system reservations\n8. setupNode()\n   a. validateSystemRequirements()                  // check cgroup subsystems; detect cpu hardcap\n   b. setupKernelTunables()                         // vm.overcommit, vm.panic_on_oom, etc.\n   c. createNodeAllocatableCgroups()                // create /kubepods cgroup\n   d. qosContainerManager.Start()                   // create burstable/besteffort cgroups\n   e. enforceNodeAllocatableCgroups()               // apply limits; retry goroutine if needed\n   f. build systemContainers list (system, kubelet) // move non-kernel PIDs; set OOM score\n9. goroutine: ensureStateFunc every 1 minute        // maintain system/kubelet cgroup membership\n10. goroutine: periodicTasks every 5 minutes        // self-detect kubelet cgroup if not configured\n11. deviceManager.Start()                           // start plugin watcher, reconcile devices\n```\n\n### 3.2 Pod Admission\n\nBefore a pod is bound to the node, the kubelet runs its chain of `PodAdmitHandler`s. The container manager contributes two:\n\n**Path A \u2014 Device allocation** (`UpdatePluginResources`, called from scheduler predicate handler):\n```\nlifecycle.PodAdmitAttributes \u2192 deviceManager.UpdatePluginResources()\n  \u2192 deviceManager.Allocate(pod, container)\n  \u2192 cached in deviceManager state\n```\n\n**Path B \u2014 Topology alignment** (`GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()` returns `topologyManager`):\n```\ntopologyManager.Admit(ctx, pod)\n  \u2192 for each container:\n      cpuManager.GetTopologyHints()    \u2192 NUMA bitmasks for CPU sets\n      memoryManager.GetTopologyHints() \u2192 NUMA bitmasks for memory\n      deviceManager.GetTopologyHints() \u2192 NUMA bitmasks for device allocations\n    \u2192 policy.Merge() \u2192 best combined hint\n    \u2192 cpuManager.Allocate()    \u2192 reserves CPUs in cpumanager state\n    \u2192 memoryManager.Allocate() \u2192 reserves NUMA nodes in memorymanager state\n    \u2192 deviceManager.Allocate() \u2192 finalizes device assignments\n```\nIf the chosen policy cannot align, `TopologyAffinityError` causes pod rejection with reason `TopologyAffinityError`.\n\n### 3.3 Container Creation\n\nCalled from `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime` when constructing the CRI `ContainerConfig`:\n\n```\nkuberuntime \u2192 cm.InternalContainerLifecycle().PreCreateContainer(pod, container, containerConfig)\n  \u2192 internalContainerLifecycleImpl.PreCreateContainer()    [Linux only]\n      cpuManager.GetCPUAffinity()   \u2192 containerConfig.Linux.Resources.CpusetCpus\n      memoryManager.GetMemoryNUMANodes() \u2192 containerConfig.Linux.Resources.CpusetMems\n```\n\nThis writes the exact CPU and memory NUMA node sets into the CRI config *before* the container runtime creates the container, so the kernel cgroup assignments are correct from the first moment.\n\n### 3.4 Container Start\n\nImmediately after the container is created and its ID is known:\n\n```\nkuberuntime \u2192 cm.InternalContainerLifecycle().PreStartContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n  \u2192 cpuManager.AddContainer()     \u2192 records containerID \u2192 (podUID, containerName) mapping\n  \u2192 memoryManager.AddContainer()  \u2192 same mapping for memory\n  \u2192 topologyManager.AddContainer()\u2192 records hint in topology store\n```\n\n### 3.5 Pod Cgroup Lifecycle\n\nThe pod workers call into `PodContainerManager` independently:\n\n```\npod admitted \u2192 podContainerManager.EnsureExists(pod)\n  \u2192 compute CgroupName: <QOS-root>/pod<uid>\n  \u2192 ResourceConfigForPod(): CPU shares/quota, memory limit, PID limit, MemoryQoS unified fields\n  \u2192 cgroupManager.Create()\n\npod terminating \u2192 podContainerManager.ReduceCPULimits()   // throttle to MinShares before kill\n               \u2192 podContainerManager.Destroy()\n                  \u2192 cgroupManager.Pids() + kill (up to 5 retries)\n                  \u2192 cgroupManager.Destroy()\n```\n\n### 3.6 Container Stop\n\n```\nkuberuntime \u2192 cm.InternalContainerLifecycle().PostStopContainer(containerID)\n  \u2192 topologyManager.RemoveContainer(containerID)\n  \u2192 (cpuManager and memoryManager remove mappings lazily via reconcile or explicit Remove)\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Hard startup failures\n\n| Condition | Location | Effect |\n|---|---|---|\n| Required cgroup subsystems not mounted (v1: cpu, cpuacct, cpuset, memory) | `container_manager_linux.go:validateSystemRequirements` | Kubelet refuses to start |\n| `--fail-swap-on=true` with swap enabled | `container_manager_linux.go:220` | Kubelet refuses to start |\n| >8 NUMA nodes with topology manager enabled | `topologymanager/topology_manager.go:41` | Kubelet refuses to start |\n| Bad `CgroupRoot` path with `CgroupsPerQOS=true` | `container_manager_linux.go:268` | Kubelet refuses to start |\n| `ProtectKernelDefaults=true` and kernel tunables are wrong | `container_manager_linux.go:setupKernelTunables` | Kubelet refuses to start |\n\n### 4.2 Soft failures at admission\n\n- **`TopologyAffinityError`**: Pod is rejected at admission. Only occurs with `restricted` or `single-numa-node` topology policies. Under `best-effort` the pod is admitted without alignment.\n- **`SMTAlignmentError`**: CPU manager static policy with `full-pcpus-only` option rejects a pod if the CPU request is not a multiple of threads-per-core, or if physical CPUs are exhausted.\n- **Device unavailability**: Device manager returns an error from `Allocate()` causing the pod to remain in `Pending`.\n\n### 4.3 Runtime degradation\n\n- **Node Allocatable enforcement retry**: If `EnforceNodeAllocatable` is set and existing memory usage already exceeds the new limit (e.g., after a live reduction), `enforceNodeAllocatableCgroups` launches a goroutine that retries the `cgroupManager.Update()` every minute, waiting for eviction to lower the node's memory usage (`node_container_manager_linux.go:95-106`).\n- **QoS memory reserve retry**: `retrySetMemoryReserve` detects a failed memory limit update by checking if current usage exceeds the attempted limit, then adjusts the limit upward to the current usage (`qos_container_manager_linux.go:265`).\n- **CPU reconciliation drift**: The CPU manager's reconcile loop periodically calls `UpdateContainerResources()` on the CRI. If a container has drifted (e.g., the runtime restarted), the reconcile corrects it. The `lastUpdateState` tracks the last successfully pushed CPUSet to avoid redundant CRI calls.\n- **cgroup v2 root cpu.stat missing**: On kernels before 5.8, the root cgroup does not expose `cpu.stat`. The kubelet logs `CgroupV2KernelWarning` and continues, but CPU accounting at the node root level will be incorrect.\n\n### 4.4 Key design tradeoffs\n\n**Interface-per-platform**: Linux gets a full `containerManagerImpl` with seven sub-managers. Windows gets a slimmer struct and skips cgroup hierarchy entirely. Unsupported builds return a stub that fails on `Start()`. This keeps the common interface clean but means platform divergence lives in separate files (`_linux.go`, `_windows.go`, `_unsupported.go`, `_stub.go`) that must be maintained in parallel.\n\n**Noop/fake fallback pattern**: Every sub-manager has a `*Noop` or `*Fake` implementation (e.g., `podContainerManagerNoop`, `qosContainerManagerNoop`, `fakeManager` in cpumanager and memorymanager). This enables tests and alternate configurations (e.g., `CgroupsPerQOS=false` silently uses noop) but also means a misconfiguration may pass validation but produce a noop that silently does nothing.\n\n**Topology manager as admission gatekeeper**: By implementing `lifecycle.PodAdmitHandler`, the topology manager blocks pod start rather than failing silently during container creation. The tradeoff is that a strict policy can permanently block pods that have no topology-aligned placement on the node.\n\n**Periodic QoS cgroup updates**: Rather than updating QoS cgroups on every pod event, the QoS manager uses a 1-minute polling interval. This simplifies the code but means a burst of new pods may temporarily cause CPU share ratios to be stale by up to one minute.\n\n**CPU Manager reconcile vs. direct assignment**: CPU pinning is a two-step process: `Allocate` reserves in the state file, then the reconcile loop pushes to the kernel. This means a container may briefly run on the shared pool if the reconcile has not yet fired after admission. The `PreCreateContainer` hook writes `CpusetCpus` into the initial `ContainerConfig`, so for newly created containers the affinity is correct from the start; the reconcile handles drift and re-alignment after restarts.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points, Customization Hooks, and Risks\n\n### 5.1 CPU Manager Policy Plugins\n\nThe `Policy` interface (`pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/policy.go`) accepts `PolicyOptions` at construction time. Operators can tune the `static` policy via `--cpu-manager-policy-options`:\n\n- `full-pcpus-only`: requires whole physical cores to be allocated together (SMT-aligned).\n- `distribute-cpus-across-numa`: spreads exclusive CPUs across NUMA nodes.\n- `align-by-socket`: aligns allocation to CPU socket boundaries.\n\nAdding a new policy requires implementing the `Policy` interface and registering it in `cpumanager.NewManager()`. Risk: incorrect policies corrupt the state file and cause incorrect CPU accounting across reboots.\n\n### 5.2 Topology Manager Policy\n\nSelectable via `--topology-manager-policy` and `--topology-manager-scope`. The `Policy` interface (`pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/policy.go`) has `Merge()` to combine hints from multiple providers. New policies can be added but must handle the full `(2^N \u2212 1)` possible NUMA bitmask combinations, which grow exponentially with NUMA node count.\n\n### 5.3 Device Plugin Registration\n\n`GetPluginRegistrationHandlers()` returns a `map[string]cache.PluginHandler` that the plugin manager's watcher passes to device plugins during socket-based registration. Adding new handler types (beyond `DevicePlugin` and `DRAPlugin`) requires changes here.\n\n### 5.4 `InternalContainerLifecycle`\n\n`InternalContainerLifecycle()` returns an `internalContainerLifecycleImpl` composed of cpu/memory/topology managers. This is the correct hook for injecting additional per-container setup that must happen before or after the CRI call. Risk: because `PreCreateContainer` writes directly into the `ContainerConfig.Linux.Resources` struct that gets sent to the CRI, errors here silently produce containers with incorrect affinity rather than failing loudly.\n\n### 5.5 `PodAdmitHandler` chain\n\n`GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()` returns the topology manager. Additional admission logic can be layered by registering more `PodAdmitHandler`s in `kubelet.go`. The topology manager must remain in the chain for device+CPU+memory co-alignment to work.\n\n### 5.6 NodeConfig knobs\n\n`NodeConfig` (`pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go:176`) is the single configuration struct that drives almost all container manager behavior. Relevant operator-facing flags:\n\n| Field | Flag | Effect |\n|---|---|---|\n| `CgroupsPerQOS` | `--cgroups-per-qos` | Enables the QoS/pod cgroup hierarchy |\n| `CgroupDriver` | `--cgroup-driver` | `systemd` or `cgroupfs`; must match the container runtime |\n| `EnforceNodeAllocatable` | `--enforce-node-allocatable` | Which cgroups to apply node-level resource limits to |\n| `CPUManagerPolicy` | `--cpu-manager-policy` | `none` (default) or `static` |\n| `TopologyManagerPolicy` | `--topology-manager-policy` | `none`, `best-effort`, `restricted`, `single-numa-node` |\n| `ProtectKernelDefaults` | `--protect-kernel-defaults` | Turn kernel tunable mismatches into startup errors |\n| `CPUCFSQuotaPeriod` | `--cpu-cfs-quota-period` | CFS period; default 100ms; lower values reduce scheduling latency at cost of overhead |\n\n---\n\n## 6. Platform Variance\n\n### Linux\n\nFull feature set. The cgroup hierarchy, QoS enforcement, CPU pinning, memory NUMA pinning, topology management, and all admission controls are active. Kernel tunables (`vm.overcommit_memory`, `vm.panic_on_oom`, `kernel.panic`, etc.) are validated or modified at startup.\n\n### Windows\n\n`pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_windows.go` defines a `containerManagerImpl` with a notably slimmer struct\u2014no cgroup fields, no QoS manager, no node allocatable enforcement. The Windows implementation:\n\n- Always returns `podContainerManagerStub{}` from `NewPodContainerManager()` (no pod-level cgroup isolation).\n- Uses fake (no-op) managers for topology, CPU, and memory by default.\n- Only activates real topology/CPU/memory managers when the `WindowsCPUAndMemoryAffinity` feature gate is enabled.\n- Starts the device manager unconditionally.\n- Has no kernel tunable setup, no swap check, no system container management.\n\n### Other/Unsupported\n\n`pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_unsupported.go` embeds `containerManagerStub` and overrides `Start()` to return `fmt.Errorf(\"Container Manager is unsupported in this build\")`. This is the build-tag fallback for non-Linux, non-Windows targets.\n\n### Stub\n\n`pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_stub.go` provides a complete no-op `ContainerManager` used in unit tests and standalone kubelet modes where resource management is intentionally disabled.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Operational Implications\n\n### 7.1 Performance\n\n**Reconcile latency**: The CPU manager reconcile loop runs at `CPUManagerReconcilePeriod` (default configurable, typically 10s). Each iteration calls `UpdateContainerResources()` once per active container for any container whose assigned CPUSet has changed since `lastUpdateState`. On large nodes with many containers, this can generate significant CRI traffic if many containers are simultaneously admitted or evicted. Operators running high-churn workloads should verify the period is not too short.\n\n**QoS CPU share accounting**: The QoS cgroup manager recomputes Burstable tier CPU shares every minute by iterating all active pods. On nodes with thousands of pods, this O(n) pass is taken under a mutex. If the node is over-subscribed and pods are constantly cycling, the 1-minute staleness window may cause persistent CPU unfairness between QoS tiers.\n\n**MilliCPU to CFS quota conversion** (`pkg/kubelet/cm/helpers_linux.go`):\n```go\nMinShares     = 2      // kernel minimum\nSharesPerCPU  = 1024   // shares per logical CPU\nQuotaPeriod   = 100000 // 100ms default CFS period\nMinQuotaPeriod = 1000  // 1ms minimum\nMinMilliCPULimit = 10  // 10m minimum CPU limit\n```\nVery small CPU limits (< 10 millicores) are clamped to `MinMilliCPULimit` to avoid kernel-rejected quota values.\n\n### 7.2 Reliability\n\n**State file durability**: Both CPU manager and memory manager persist their allocation state to files in `KubeletRootDir`. On kubelet restart, state is re-read and reconciled against the live container set obtained from the CRI. Containers present in the state file but absent from the CRI are cleaned up; containers in the CRI but absent from state are re-assigned to the shared pool (for CPU) or re-evaluated (for memory). The state file uses JSON and is not atomic-write protected by default; a partial write during a crash could corrupt state and require manual recovery.\n\n**Cgroup creation idempotency**: `EnsureExists` checks `cgroupManager.Exists()` before calling `Create()`, making it safe to call repeatedly. However, `Destroy()` may fail to remove cgroups if zombie processes hold file descriptors within the cgroup namespace, leaving orphan cgroups that prevent future creation of cgroups with the same name (same pod UID). The `tryKillingCgroupProcesses` helper retries up to five times to kill all processes before the cgroup is removed.\n\n**Enforcement goroutine**: When Node Allocatable enforcement fails because current usage exceeds the new limit, the retry goroutine sleeps for 1 minute between attempts with no backoff cap. This means the goroutine runs indefinitely if the node is persistently over its new allocatable limit\u2014expected behavior while eviction is in progress, but leaks a goroutine permanently if eviction never succeeds.\n\n### 7.3 Maintainability\n\n**Platform divergence debt**: Three parallel `containerManagerImpl` structs (Linux, Windows, stub) share the same `ContainerManager` interface but implement very different subsets of it. Adding new interface methods requires stubs across all implementations. The mock generation (`//go:generate mockery` in `container_manager.go`) helps with test coverage but does not eliminate the drift risk.\n\n**Cgroup v1 deprecation trajectory**: Cgroup v1 support is explicitly deprecated with a logged warning at startup and an active KEP (sig-node/5573-remove-cgroup-v1). The v1 manager code (`cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go`) will be removed in a future release. Clusters still using v1 should migrate to v2 before this occurs.\n\n**Resource update channel fan-in**: The constructor builds a fan-in goroutine that merges update channels from `deviceManager` and `draManager` into a single `cm.resourceUpdates` channel (buffer 10). The channel is closed when all sources close. This design assumes the two sources have compatible lifecycles; if either source's channel is never closed (e.g., due to a manager panic), the fan-in goroutine leaks.\n\n---\n\n## 8. File and Directory Map\n\n```\npkg/kubelet/cm/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 container_manager.go              # ContainerManager interface, NodeConfig, NodeAllocatableConfig, Status\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 container_manager_linux.go        # containerManagerImpl (Linux): construction, Start(), all sub-manager wiring\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 container_manager_windows.go      # containerManagerImpl (Windows): slimmer struct, feature-gated CPU/memory\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 container_manager_stub.go         # containerManagerStub: no-op, used in tests\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 container_manager_unsupported.go  # unsupportedContainerManager: errors on Start()\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 types.go                          # CgroupName, CgroupConfig, ResourceConfig, CgroupManager, PodContainerManager interfaces\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 cgroup_manager_linux.go           # CgroupName \u2194 systemd/cgroupfs translation; CPU/memory affinity written into `ContainerConfig` via `InternalContainerLifecycle` |\n    27\t| `pkg/kubelet/eviction` | Node allocatable values used for eviction thresholds |\n    28\t| `pkg/kubelet/server` (PodResources API) | CPU, device, memory, DRA data via `CPUsProvider`, `DevicesProvider`, `MemoryProvider`, `DynamicResourcesProvider` interfaces |\n    29\t| `pkg/kubelet/nodestatus` | `GetCapacity()`, `GetDevicePluginResourceCapacity()`, `GetNodeAllocatableReservation()` |\n    30\t| Linux kernel cgroup filesystem | Cgroup directories, quota files, CPU shares, memory limits |\n    31\t\n    32\t---\n    33\t\n    34\t## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n    35\t\n    36\tThe subsystem is a single Go package (`pkg/kubelet/cm`) that composes six major sub-managers. Each has a narrow Go interface and the `ContainerManager` orchestrates them.\n    37\t\n    38\t### 2.1 `ContainerManager` (the orchestrator)\n    39\t\n    40\t**Interface**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go`, type `ContainerManager`\n    41\t\n    42\t`containerManagerImpl` (Linux) holds references to all sub-managers and is the only type exposed to the rest of the kubelet:\n    43\t\n    44\t```go\n    45\t// pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go:100-140\n    46\ttype containerManagerImpl struct {\n    47\t    sync.RWMutex\n    48\t    cadvisorInterface cadvisor.Interface\n    49\t    cgroupManager     CgroupManager\n    50\t    qosContainerManager QOSContainerManager\n    51\t    deviceManager     devicemanager.Manager\n    52\t    cpuManager        cpumanager.Manager\n    53\t    memoryManager     memorymanager.Manager\n    54\t    topologyManager   topologymanager.Manager\n    55\t    draManager        *dra.Manager\n    56\t    // ...\n    57\t}\n    58\t```\n    59\t\n    60\tIts responsibilities include:\n    61\t- Construction and sequential initialization of all sub-managers\n    62\t- Kernel tunable validation (`setupKernelTunables`, `ProtectKernelDefaults`)\n    63\t- Cgroup root setup and Node Allocatable enforcement\n    64\t- Fanning-in resource-update channels from device manager and DRA manager\n    65\t- Exposing the PodResources API data plane\n    66\t\n    67\t### 2.2 `CgroupManager`\n    68\t\n    69\t**Interface**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go`, type `CgroupManager`  \n    70\t**Implementations**: `cgroup_manager_linux.go` (shared), `cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go`, `cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go`\n    71\t\n    72\tPerforms the raw cgroup operations: `Create`, `Destroy`, `Update`, `Validate`, `Exists`, `MemoryUsage`, `Pids`, and `ReduceCPULimits`. Its `Name()` method translates the internal `CgroupName` (a `[]string` slice like `[\"kubepods\",\"burstable\",\"pod<uid>\"]`) into the driver-specific filesystem path. For the systemd driver it uses `cgroupsystemd.ExpandSlice()` to produce `/kubepods.slice/kubepods-burstable.slice/kubepods-burstable-pod<uid>.slice`; for the cgroupfs driver it joins with `/`.\n    73\t\n    74\tThe `NewCgroupManager` factory selects `cgroupV1impl` or `cgroupV2impl` based on `cgroups.IsCgroup2UnifiedMode()`. Cgroup v1 is actively deprecated\u2014a warning is emitted at startup:\n    75\t\n    76\t```go\n    77\t// pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go:52\n    78\tCgroupV1DeprecatedWarning = \"cgroup v1 detected. cgroup v1 support is deprecated...\"\n    79\t```\n    80\t\n    81\t### 2.3 `QOSContainerManager`\n    82\t\n    83\t**Interface**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/qos_container_manager_linux.go`, type `QOSContainerManager`  \n    84\t**Implementation**: `qosContainerManagerImpl`\n    85\t\n    86\tCreates and maintains the three top-level QoS tier cgroups under the cgroup root. The Guaranteed tier lives *at* the cgroup root itself; Burstable and BestEffort each get a child:\n    87\t\n    88\t```\n    89\t/kubepods            \u2190 Guaranteed (= cgroupRoot)\n    90\t/kubepods/burstable\n    91\t/kubepods/besteffort\n    92\t```\n    93\t\n    94\tOn startup it creates any missing QoS cgroups and then launches a goroutine that calls `UpdateCgroups` every `1 minute` (`periodicQOSCgroupUpdateInterval`). Each update recomputes:\n    95\t\n    96\t- **CPU shares** for Burstable: sums all Burstable pod CPU requests; `MilliCPUToShares()` converts them (`SharesPerCPU = 1024` per CPU, `MinShares = 2`).\n    97\t- **Memory limits** (when `QOSReserved` feature is enabled): calculates tier memory limits as `allocatable \u2212 (guaranteed_requests \u00d7 percentReserve / 100)` with a retry mechanism that raises the limit to current usage if the cgroup is already over the desired limit.\n    98\t- **MemoryQoS** (`memory.min`, cgroup v2 only, `MemoryQoS` feature): sets `memory.min` to prevent the OS from reclaiming memory below the sum of all pod requests in the tier.\n    99\t\n   100\t### 2.4 `PodContainerManager`\n   101\t\n   102\t**Interface**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go`, type `PodContainerManager`  \n   103\t**Linux implementation**: `pod_container_manager_linux.go`, type `podContainerManagerImpl`  \n   104\t**Fallback**: `podContainerManagerNoop` (when `CgroupsPerQOS=false`)\n   105\t\n   106\tThe pod workers call `EnsureExists()` before starting containers and `Destroy()` when a pod terminates. `EnsureExists` computes the pod cgroup name as `<QOS-parent>/pod<uid>`, derives a `ResourceConfig` from the pod spec via `ResourceConfigForPod()` (CPU shares, quota, memory limits, PID limits), and calls `cgroupManager.Create()`. Destruction first kills all processes attached to the cgroup with up to five retry rounds, then removes the cgroup.\n   107\t\n   108\tA key feature interaction: if `DisableCPUQuotaWithExclusiveCPUs` is enabled and the pod has pinned CPUs (checked via `ContainerManager.PodHasExclusiveCPUs()`), `EnsureExists` disables CFS quota for that pod cgroup, preventing quota interference with pinned workloads.\n   109\t\n   110\t### 2.5 CPU Manager\n   111\t\n   112\t**Interface**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/cpu_manager.go`, type `Manager`  \n   113\t**Implementation**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/cpu_manager.go`, type `manager`\n   114\t\n   115\tManages CPU affinity for containers through a pluggable policy:\n   116\t\n   117\t- **`none` policy** (`policy_none.go`): All containers use the shared CPU pool. All topology hints report no preference.\n   118\t- **`static` policy** (`policy_static.go`): Guaranteed pods requesting an integer number of CPUs receive exclusively dedicated logical CPUs. Containers from all other classes share the remaining pool. The static policy also supports SMT-alignment: it can require requests to be multiples of threads-per-core (`full-pcpus-only` option).\n   119\t\n   120\tState (the `podUID \u2192 containerName \u2192 CPUSet` mapping) is persisted to `cpu_manager_state` in `KubeletRootDir` so that CPU allocations survive kubelet restarts. A periodic reconcile loop calls `UpdateContainerResources()` on the CRI to push the current CPUSet into every container's cgroup, healing any drift.\n   121\t\n   122\tThe CPU manager implements `topologymanager.HintProvider`; when the topology manager calls `GetTopologyHints()`, the CPU manager returns possible NUMA-local CPU sets as bitmasks.\n   123\t\n   124\t### 2.6 Memory Manager\n   125\t\n   126\t**Interface**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/`, type `Manager`  \n   127\t**Implementation**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/memory_manager.go`\n   128\t\n   129\tMirrors the CPU manager's structure for NUMA-aware memory allocation. For Guaranteed pods it pins memory to specific NUMA nodes by writing `cpuset.mems` into the container's cgroup. State is also persisted to disk. It implements `HintProvider` and cooperates with the topology manager on placement decisions.\n   130\t\n   131\t### 2.7 Topology Manager\n   132\t\n   133\t**Interface**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/topology_manager.go`, type `Manager`  \n   134\t**Implementation**: `topology_manager.go` + `scope.go` + policy files\n   135\t\n   136\tThe topology manager acts as an **admission controller** for NUMA alignment. It implements `lifecycle.PodAdmitHandler`, meaning it is called during pod admission (`GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()` returns it).\n   137\t\n   138\tAt admission time it:\n   139\t1. Calls `GetTopologyHints(pod, container)` on every registered `HintProvider` (device manager, CPU manager, memory manager).\n   140\t2. Intersects the returned bitmask sets using the configured policy.\n   141\t3. Calls `Allocate(pod, container)` on each provider to commit resources matching the agreed hint.\n   142\t\n   143\tPolicies:\n   144\t- `none`: alignment is not enforced; hints are ignored.\n   145\t- `best-effort`: prefers aligned placement; admits the pod even if alignment is impossible.\n   146\t- `restricted`: only admits pods that can be placed with NUMA affinity.\n   147\t- `single-numa-node`: only admits pods whose resources all fit on a single NUMA node.\n   148\t\n   149\tScopes (`container` / `pod`) control whether alignment is computed per container or across the whole pod. The `noneScope` is used when the policy is `none`.\n   150\t\n   151\t**Hard limit**: The topology manager refuses to initialize on machines with more than 8 NUMA nodes because the hint enumeration would produce a state explosion (`defaultMaxAllowableNUMANodes = 8`).\n   152\t\n   153\t### 2.8 Device Manager\n   154\t\n   155\t**Directory**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/`\n   156\t\n   157\tManages device plugin registrations, allocations, and health monitoring. Exposes `GetWatcherHandler()` (registered with the plugin manager) and `GetCapacity()` (feeds node status). Device allocations are bundled into `RunContainerOptions` by `GetResources()`.\n   158\t\n   159\t### 2.9 DRA Manager\n   160\t\n   161\t**Directory**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/dra/`  \n   162\t**Feature gate**: `DynamicResourceAllocation`\n   163\t\n   164\tImplements the newer structured resource allocation model. Communicates with DRA drivers via gRPC and stores claim state in checkpoints. Exposes a `GetWatcherHandler()` similar to the device manager.\n   165\t\n   166\t---\n   167\t\n   168\t## 3. End-to-End Control Flow\n   169\t\n   170\t### 3.1 Initialization (`Start()`)\n   171\t\n   172\t`containerManagerImpl.Start()` is called once from `Kubelet.Run()` after the node is registered. The Linux sequence (`pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go:615`):\n   173\t\n   174\t```\n   175\t1. buildContainerMapAndRunningSetFromRuntime()      // enumerate live containers via CRI\n   176\t2. draManager.Start()                               // if DynamicResourceAllocation enabled\n   177\t3. cpuManager.Start()                               // loads persisted state, starts reconcile loop\n   178\t4. memoryManager.Start()                            // loads persisted state, starts reconcile loop\n   179\t5. cm.nodeInfo = node                               // cache node object\n   180\t6. cadvisor.RootFsInfo() \u2192 cm.capacity              // populate ephemeral-storage capacity\n   181\t7. validateNodeAllocatable()                         // sanity-check kube/system reservations\n   182\t8. setupNode()\n   183\t   a. validateSystemRequirements()                  // check cgroup subsystems; detect cpu hardcap\n   184\t   b. setupKernelTunables()                         // vm.overcommit, vm.panic_on_oom, etc.\n   185\t   c. createNodeAllocatableCgroups()                // create /kubepods cgroup\n   186\t   d. qosContainerManager.Start()                   // create burstable/besteffort cgroups\n   187\t   e. enforceNodeAllocatableCgroups()               // apply limits; retry goroutine if needed\n   188\t   f. build systemContainers list (system, kubelet) // move non-kernel PIDs; set OOM score\n   189\t9. goroutine: ensureStateFunc every 1 minute        // maintain system/kubelet cgroup membership\n   190\t10. goroutine: periodicTasks every 5 minutes        // self-detect kubelet cgroup if not configured\n   191\t11. deviceManager.Start()                           // start plugin watcher, reconcile devices\n   192\t```\n   193\t\n   194\t### 3.2 Pod Admission\n   195\t\n   196\tBefore a pod is bound to the node, the kubelet runs its chain of `PodAdmitHandler`s. The container manager contributes two:\n   197\t\n   198\t**Path A \u2014 Device allocation** (`UpdatePluginResources`, called from scheduler predicate handler):\n   199\t```\n   200\tlifecycle.PodAdmitAttributes \u2192 deviceManager.UpdatePluginResources()\n   201\t  \u2192 deviceManager.Allocate(pod, container)\n   202\t  \u2192 cached in deviceManager state\n   203\t```\n   204\t\n   205\t**Path B \u2014 Topology alignment** (`GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()` returns `topologyManager`):\n   206\t```\n   207\ttopologyManager.Admit(ctx, pod)\n   208\t  \u2192 for each container:\n   209\t      cpuManager.GetTopologyHints()    \u2192 NUMA bitmasks for CPU sets\n   210\t      memoryManager.GetTopologyHints() \u2192 NUMA bitmasks for memory\n   211\t      deviceManager.GetTopologyHints() \u2192 NUMA bitmasks for device allocations\n   212\t    \u2192 policy.Merge() \u2192 best combined hint\n   213\t    \u2192 cpuManager.Allocate()    \u2192 reserves CPUs in cpumanager state\n   214\t    \u2192 memoryManager.Allocate() \u2192 reserves NUMA nodes in memorymanager state\n   215\t    \u2192 deviceManager.Allocate() \u2192 finalizes device assignments\n   216\t```\n   217\tIf the chosen policy cannot align, `TopologyAffinityError` causes pod rejection with reason `TopologyAffinityError`.\n   218\t\n   219\t### 3.3 Container Creation\n   220\t\n   221\tCalled from `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime` when constructing the CRI `ContainerConfig`:\n   222\t\n   223\t```\n   224\tkuberuntime \u2192 cm.InternalContainerLifecycle().PreCreateContainer(pod, container, containerConfig)\n   225\t  \u2192 internalContainerLifecycleImpl.PreCreateContainer()    [Linux only]\n   226\t      cpuManager.GetCPUAffinity()   \u2192 containerConfig.Linux.Resources.CpusetCpus\n   227\t      memoryManager.GetMemoryNUMANodes() \u2192 containerConfig.Linux.Resources.CpusetMems\n   228\t```\n   229\t\n   230\tThis writes the exact CPU and memory NUMA node sets into the CRI config *before* the container runtime creates the container, so the kernel cgroup assignments are correct from the first moment.\n   231\t\n   232\t### 3.4 Container Start\n   233\t\n   234\tImmediately after the container is created and its ID is known:\n   235\t\n   236\t```\n   237\tkuberuntime \u2192 cm.InternalContainerLifecycle().PreStartContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n   238\t  \u2192 cpuManager.AddContainer()     \u2192 records containerID \u2192 (podUID, containerName) mapping\n   239\t  \u2192 memoryManager.AddContainer()  \u2192 same mapping for memory\n   240\t  \u2192 topologyManager.AddContainer()\u2192 records hint in topology store\n   241\t```\n   242\t\n   243\t### 3.5 Pod Cgroup Lifecycle\n   244\t\n   245\tThe pod workers call into `PodContainerManager` independently:\n   246\t\n   247\t```\n   248\tpod admitted \u2192 podContainerManager.EnsureExists(pod)\n   249\t  \u2192 compute CgroupName: <QOS-root>/pod<uid>\n   250\t  \u2192 ResourceConfigForPod(): CPU shares/quota, memory limit, PID limit, MemoryQoS unified fields\n   251\t  \u2192 cgroupManager.Create()\n   252\t\n   253\tpod terminating \u2192 podContainerManager.ReduceCPULimits()   // throttle to MinShares before kill\n   254\t               \u2192 podContainerManager.Destroy()\n   255\t                  \u2192 cgroupManager.Pids() + kill (up to 5 retries)\n   256\t                  \u2192 cgroupManager.Destroy()\n   257\t```\n   258\t\n   259\t### 3.6 Container Stop\n   260\t\n   261\t```\n   262\tkuberuntime \u2192 cm.InternalContainerLifecycle().PostStopContainer(containerID)\n   263\t  \u2192 topologyManager.RemoveContainer(containerID)\n   264\t  \u2192 (cpuManager and memoryManager remove mappings lazily via reconcile or explicit Remove)\n   265\t```\n   266\t\n   267\t---\n   268\t\n   269\t## 4.
